Clause Remarks Information/Comments
1.3 Collateral standards The equipment has been evaluated also according to
collateral standard IEC 60601-1-6:2010 + AMD1:2013 +
AMD2:2020, see attachment 3.
4.2 Risk management process RM Results are documented by the manufacturer on the
basis of ISO 14971:2019 and EN ISO 14971:2019/A11:
2021 referring to the OD-2044-1 (ed.1.0) from IECEE,
and are reviewed by Nemko.
4.8 Components The power supply box, model DEPS9601 and
DEPS9601A have been separately tested and certified by
Nemko (CBTC No. NO82590/A1/M2 and NO96755/M1)
according to IEC 60601-1:2005 + AMD1:2012, refer to
appended table 8.10.
The AC/DC adapter, model BM090S15F has been
separately tested and certified by UL (CBTC No. DK-
51428-A1-M1-UL) according to IEC 60601-1:2005 +
AMD1:2012, refer to appended table 8.10.
The rechargeable Li-ion battery, model SDB-3S1PA has
been separately tested and certified by TÜV Rh (CBTC
No. JPTUV-114329-M1) according to IEC 62133-2:2017,
refer to appended table 8.10.
These test report were reviewed and found to be
acceptable. Acceptance of these test reports is at the
discretion of the accepting NCB or agency.
6 Classification The equipment has the following classifications:
- Type of protection against electric shock:
● Class I for power supply box and AC/DC adapter
● Internally powered for detector
- Degree of protection against electric shock (Patient
connections): Type B applied part for front panel of
detector
- Degree of protection against harmful ingress of water or
particulate matter: Ordinary equipment (IPX0)
- Methods of sterilization: The equipment is not intended
to be sterilized by operator.
- Degree of safety application for use in an oxygen
environment: Not applicable.
- Mode of operation: Continuous operation
7 Identification, markings and
documents
Markings and instructions related to the safety shall be in
a language which is acceptable in the country in which
the equipment is to be sold. Markings and instructions in
English were evaluated in this test report.

General product information and other remarks:
This test report No. REP032757 replaces the previous original test report No. 397950 and
amendment test report No. 438157 due to updating the standard version to IEC 60601-1:2005 +
AMD1:2012 to IEC 60601-1:2005 + AMD1:2012 + AMD2:2020, and covers technical modifications as
following:
- Updating the standard version by adding AMD2:2020 to IEC 60601-1-6:2010 + AMD1:2013
(see attachment 3).
- Modified the address of applicant, manufacturer and factory (see bold letters on page 1, 13
and copy of marking plate).
- Modifying the electrical rating due to adding AC/DC adapter, model BM090S15F for power
configuration 2 (see bold letters on page 2).
- Adding the AC/DC adapter, model BM090S15F intended to be used as alternative component
of power supply box (see bold letters in copy of marking plate and appended table 8.10).
After reviewing of the above updates concerned, this amendment test report was checked with the
following:
Cl. 4.11 Power input
Cl. 5.7 Humidity preconditioning treatment
Cl. 8.7 Leakage current measurement
Cl. 8.8.3 Dielectric strength test
Cl. 8.9 Creepage distance and air clearances
Cl. 11.1.1 Excessive temperature
Unless otherwise stated, all testing was conducted with the flat digital flat panel X-ray detector,
type HAD1717MCW.
The equipment is indicated for digital imaging solution designed for providing general radiographic
diagnosis of human anatomy targeting both adult and children. It is intended to replace film based
radiographic diagnostic systems. But the equipment is not intended to be used for mammography.
The equipment consists of external power supply (power supply box or AC/DC adapter), digital flat panel
X-ray detector, switch box and exposure switch. The external power supply (power supply box or AC/DC
adapter) and digital flat panel X-ray detector are intended for use with patient environment. The switch box
and exposure switch are intended for use outside patient environment.
The equipment provides two kinds of power configuration, refer to following configuration for each power
configuration:
- Power configuration 1: Power supply box, data cable (rating of detector: 3 A, 16 Vdc)
- Power configuration 2: AC/DC adapter, ethernet cable (rating of detector: 6 A, 15 Vdc)

Page 15 of 189 Report No. REP032757
TRF No. IEC60601_1U
General product information and other remarks: (Continued)
The equipment is generally used with X-ray equipment / system including operating PC in end-use
application. Refer to below set-up diagrams which are intended by the manufacturer.
- AED mode (Without switch box)
- Normal mode (with switch box)
Based on above set-up diagrams, further consideration shall be checked as following when the equipment
is used in the end-use application.
- The suitability of the mounting means shall be tested and evaluated.
- The compliance shall be tested and evaluated when the equipment constitutes as ME system in the
end-use application.
- X-ray equipment / system shall be powered from separate mains supply which complies with IEC
60601-1.
- Operation PC shall be powered from separate mains supply which complies with IEC 60601-1 or
IEC 60950-1.
All testing was conducted with the PC submitted by manufacturer (Type: Latitude, manufactured by Dell
Inc.), since it doesn’t provide in the product package, Therefore, the equipment should be considered
whether the compliance needs to be additionally tested evaluated, when it constitutes as the ME system
with other equipment which is not verified in this test report.

Page 16 of 189 Report No. REP032757
TRF No. IEC60601_1U
General product information and other remarks: (Continued)
The equipment provides the battery recharger and recharger adapter in the product package. Those
components are intended to be used outside of patient environment and certified according to IEC 60950-
1. Therefore, those components are not tested and evaluated in this test report.
Model differences:
- The main model is HAD1717MCW.
- The variants HAD1417MCW are identical to main model HAD1717MCW except for model name,
dimension, weight, total pixel number, total pixel area, effective pixel number and effective pixel
area as below table:
Model name HAD1717MCW HAD1417MCW
Dimension (W x L x H, mm) 460 x 460 x 15 384 x 460 x 15
Weight (kg) Approx. 3.7 Approx. 3.5
Total pixel number (pixels) 3072 x 3072 2560 x 3072
Total pixel area (mm) 430 x 430 358.5 x 430
Effective pixel number (pixels) 3036 x 3040 2466 x 3040
Effective pixel area (mm) 425.04 x 425.6 345.24 x 425.6
Unless otherwise specified, all testing was conducted with main model HAD1717MCW as representative.
National Differences:
- Korea national differences (the latest edition) aligned with IEC 60601-1:2005 + AMD1:2012 was
applied and attached in this test report for information only since Korea national differences
aligned with IEC 60601-1:2005 + AMD1:2012 + AMD2:2020 has not been declared.
This test report is not related to KS Q ISO/IEC 17025 and KOLAS accreditation.

Supplementary Information:
1) Multiplication factor (1.14 for MOOP) is applied for altitude up to 3000 m based on table 8.
2) Highest working voltage, minimum measured creepage and minimum measured air clearance are
taken from the IEC 60601-1 test report of power supply box.
3) Short-circuit testing was considered due to the insufficient insulation distance. Leakage current testing
was performed during short-circuit in order to show no hazard in this area, see appended table 8.7.
4) Highest working voltage, minimum measured creepage and minimum measured air clearance are
taken from the IEC 60601-1 test report of AC/DC adapter.

Page 20 of 189 Report No. REP032757
IEC 60601-1
Clause Requirement + Test Result - Remark Verdict
TRF No. IEC60601_1U
INSULATION DIAGRAM CONVENTIONS and GUIDANCE:
A measured value must be provided in the value columns for the device under evaluation. The
symbol > (greater than sign) must not be used. Switch-mode power supplies must be re-evaluated in
the device under evaluation therefore N/A must not be used with a generic statement that the
component is certified.
Insulation diagram is a graphical representation of equipment insulation barriers, protective
impedance and protective earthing. If feasible, use the following conventions to generate the
diagram:
- All isolation barriers are identified by letters between separate parts of diagram, for example separate
transformer
windings, optocouplers, wire insulation, creepage and clearance distances.
- Parts connected to earth with large dots are protectively earthed. Other connections to earth are functional
- Applied parts are extended beyond the equipment enclosure and terminated with an arrow.
- Parts accessible to the operator only are extended outside of the enclosure but are not terminated with an
arrow.

Attachment - Software – IEC 62304:2006+AMD1:2015 —
4.3 [A, B, C] Software safety classification —
a) The MANUFACTURER assigns to each SOFTWARE
SYSTEM a software safety class according to the RISK
of HARM to the patient, operator, or other people
resulting from a HAZARDOUS SITUATION to which the
SOFTWARE SYSTEM can contribute in a worst-case-
scenario
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046), chapter 1
P
The SOFTWARE SYSTEM is software safety class A if: —
– the SOFTWARE SYSTEM not contribute to a
HAZARDOUS SITUATION; or
Classified as software class B. N/A
– the SOFTWARE SYSTEM contribute to a HAZARDOUS
SITUATION which does not result in unacceptable
RISK after consideration of RISK CONTROL measures
external to the SOFTWARE SYSTEM
N/A
The SOFTWARE SYSTEM is software safety class B if: —
– the SOFTWARE SYSTEM contribute to a HAZARDOUS
SITUATION which results in unacceptable RISK after
consideration of RISK CONTROL measures external to
the SOFTWARE SYSTEM and the resulting possible
HARM is non-SERIOUS INJURY
P
The SOFTWARE SYSTEM is software safety class C if: —
– the SOFTWARE SYSTEM contribute to a HAZARDOUS
SITUATION which results in unacceptable RISK after
consideration of RISK CONTROL measures external to
the SOFTWARE SYSTEM and the resulting possible
HARM is death or SERIOUS INJURY
Classified as software class B. N/A
For a SOFTWARE SYSTEM initially classified as
software safety class B or C, the MANUFACTURER
has implemented additional RISK CONTROL measures
external to the SOFTWARE SYSTEM and subsequently
has assigned a new software safety classification to
the SOFTWARE SYSTEM
N/A
c) The MANUFACTURER documents the software
safety class assigned to each SOFTWARE SYSTEM in
the RISK MANAGEMENT FILE
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046), chapter 1
P
d) When a SOFTWARE SYSTEM is decomposed into
SOFTWARE ITEMS, and when a SOFTWARE ITEM is
decomposed into further SOFTWARE ITEMS, such
SOFTWARE ITEMS inherit the software safety
classification of the original SOFTWARE ITEM (or
SOFTWARE SYSTEM) unless the MANUFACTURER
documents a rationale for classification into a
different software safety class
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046), chapter 1
P
A rationale explains how the new SOFTWARE ITEMS
are segregated so that they may be classified
separately
. P

Page 173 of 189 Report No. REP032757
IEC 60601-1
Clause Requirement + Test Result - Remark Verdict
TRF No. IEC60601_1U
e) The MANUFACTURER documents the software
safety class of each SOFTWARE ITEM if that class is
different from the class of the SOFTWARE ITEM from
which it was created by decomposition
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046), chapter 1
P
f) When applied to a group of SOFTWARE ITEMS, the
MANUFACTURER uses the PROCESSES and TASKS
which are required by the classification of the
highest-classified SOFTWARE ITEM in the group
unless the MANUFACTURER documents in the RISK
MANAGEMENT FILE a rationale for using a lower
classification
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046), chapter 1
P

SYSTEM, until a software safety class is assigned
Classified as software class B. N/A

7.1.1 [B, C] The MANUFACTURER identifies SOFTWARE ITEMS
that could contribute to a hazardous situation
identified in the MEDICAL DEVICE RISK ANALYSIS
ACTIVITY of ISO 14971
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046), chapter 11
P
7.1.2 [B, C] The MANUFACTURER identifies potential causes
of the SOFTWARE ITEM identified above contributing
to a hazardous situation
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046), chapter 11
P
The MANUFACTURER considers potential causes including, as appropriate: P
a) incorrect or incomplete specification of
functionality
P
b) software defects in the identified SOFTWARE ITEM
functionality
P
c) failure or unexpected results from SOUP N/A
d) hardware failures or other software defects that
could result in unpredictable software operation
P
e) reasonably foreseeable misuse P
7.1.3 [B, C] If failure or unexpected results from SOUP is a
potential cause of the SOFTWARE ITEM contributing to
a hazardous situation, the MANUFACTURER
EVALUATES as a minimum any ANOMALY list
published by the supplier of the SOUP item relevant
to the VERSION of the SOUP item used in the MEDICAL
DEVICE to determine if any of the known ANOMALIES
result in a sequence of events that could result in a
hazardous situation

9 SOFTWARE PROBLEM RESOLUTION PROCESS —
9.1 [A, B, C] The MANUFACTURER prepares a PROBLEM
REPORT for each problem detected in the MEDICAL
DEVICE SOFTWARE
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046), chapter 8.3
P
PROBLEM REPORTS include a statement of criticality
(for example, effect on performance, SAFETY, or
SECURITY) as well as other information that may aid
in the resolution of the problem (for example,
devices affected, supported accessories affected)
P
9.2 [A, B, C] The MANUFACTURER: P
a) investigates the problem and if possible identify
the causes
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046), chapter 8.3
P
b) EVALUATES the problem’s relevance to SAFETY
using the software RISK MANAGEMENT PROCESS
P
c) documents the outcome of the investigation and
evaluation
P
d) creates a CHANGE REQUEST(S) for actions needed
to correct the problem, or document the rationale for
taking no action
P
9.3 [A, B, C] The MANUFACTURER advises relevant
parties of the existence of the problem, as
appropriate
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046), chapter 8.3
P

implements all CHANGE REQUESTS, observing the
requirements of the change control PROCESS
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046), chapter 8.3
P

VERIFICATION
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046), chapter 8.3
P

FILE as appropriate
P

detect trends in PROBLEM REPORTS
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046), chapter 8.3
P

a) problem has been resolved and the PROBLEM
REPORT has been closed
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046), chapter 8.3
P

c) CHANGE REQUESTS have been implemented in the
appropriate MEDICAL DEVICE SOFTWARE and
ACTIVITIES
P

Exception:
Fixed and stationary X-ray ME EQUIPMENT supplied
from a branch circuit rated at 30 A or less, and ME
EQUIPMENT that is not strictly portable but obviously
is intended to be stationary, may be acceptable if
provided with a length of attached hard service
flexible cord - such as Type S, or the equivalent,
for supply connection.
N/A
The installation of connecting cords between
EQUIPMENT parts meets the requirements of the
NEC, as applicable. Cable used as external
interconnection between units are as follows:
N/A
1) If exposed to abuse, the cables are Type SJT,
SJTO, SJO, ST, SO, STO, or equivalent flexible
cord or similar multiple-conductor appliance-wiring
material such as computer cable
N/A
2) If not exposed to abuse, the cables are as
indicated in item 1) above or are:
i) Type SPT-2, SP-2, or SPE-2, or equivalent,
ii) Type SVr, SVRO, SVE, or equivalent flexible
cord or similar multiple-conductor appliance
wiring material, or
iii) An assembly of insulated wires each with a
nominal insulation thickness of 0.8 mm (1/32 inch)
or more, enclosed in acceptable insulating tubing
having a nominal wall thickness of 0.8 mm (1/32
inch) or more.
N/A

ME SYSTEMS for use in the patient care areas of
paediatric wards, rooms, or areas are listed
tamper resistant or employ a listed tamper
resistant cover in accordance with the NEC.
N/A
b) For ME EQUIPMENT provided with NEMA
configuration non-locking plug types 120 V/15 A,

Grade” mains plug is provided and the POWER
SUPPLY CORD is marked.

This Standard applies to the BASIC SAFETY and
ESSENTIAL PERFORMANCE of MEDICAL ELECTRICAL
EQUIPMENT and MEDICAL ELECTRICAL SYSTEMS
designed to be used in accordance with CSA C22.1
(Canadian Electrical Code, Part I) and CSA Z32.
Considered. P

Canadian standards may modify, replace, or delete requirements contained in the
IEC standard as appropriate to the ME EQUIPMENT and ME SYSTEMS under evaluation,
and they may add other BASIC SAFETY and ESSENTIAL PERFORMANCE requirements
—

and any part that is PROTECTIVELY EARTHED
shall not exceed 100 mΩ…………………………..:

REP032757.
P

connection to ME EQUIPMENT, the earth pin of
the APPLIANCE INLET is regarded as the
PROTECTIVE EARTH TERMINAL.

requirements as described in IEC 60601-1.
Separate testing is required to comply with CSA
C22.2 No. 0.4.

Testing shall be carried out using a DETACHABLE
POWER SUPPLY CORD as provided or specified

(length and cross-sectional area as per the
Canadian Electrical Code, Part I) by the
MANUFACTURER.
P
The test current shall have the following
characteristics:
— for cord-connected equipment, twice the rating
of the attachment plug cap, but not less than 40 A;
— for equipment for permanent connection to the
supply, twice the rating of the fuse that is required
by the Canadian Electrical Code, Part I for the
branch circuit to which the equipment is
connected, up to 250 A; and
— 500 A for equipment for permanent connection
to the supply when a branch circuit fused at over
250 A is required.
See appended table 8.6.4 in
part 1 original test report No.
REP032757.
P
Compliance is checked by the following test:
— for test currents up to 500 A, the measured
potential drop shall not exceed 4 V;
— for equipment that requires branch circuit fusing
over 250 A, the measured potential drop multiplied
by the required fusing and divided by 250 shall not
exceed 4 V;
— there shall be no melting of any metal in the
bond and no heating or burning that is likely to
create a fire hazard; and
— the time duration— the time duration for testing
is indicated in Table 8.6.4A:
N/A
P
Alternatively, dc may be used for this test, if the
ME EQUIPMENT is rated dc. N/A

National Differences
Page 13 of 33
Report No.: REP032757
IEC60601_1U ATTACHMENT
Clause Requirement + Test Result - Remark Verdict
Note: When protective earth is relied on as a
MEANS OF PROTECTION, the test current is
determined based on the location where a fault
could occur. If the prospective fault is in the mains
supply circuit prior to the overcurrent protection
included in the ME EQUIPMENT, the test current
for that part of the protective earth circuit is based
on the rating of the external overcurrent protection
included in the building infrastructure or specified
in the ACCOMPANYING DOCUMENTS (two times
the interrupt rating of the external overcurrent
protection). If the prospective fault is in the mains
supply circuit after the overcurrent protection
included in the ME EQUIPMENT, the
test current is based on the rating of the
overcurrent protection included in the ME
EQUIPMENT (two times the interrupt rating of the
ME EQUIPMENT overcurrent protection). In either
case, the minimum test current is 40 A.
The voltage drop between the parts described is
measured and the impedance determined from the
current and voltage drop.
If the measured impedance is within the permitted
limit, either the impedance measurement is then
repeated using a current source with a no-load
voltage sufficient to deliver the specified current
into the total impedance, or the current-carrying
ability of the relevant protective earth conductor
and protective earth connection is confirmed by
checking that their cross-sectional area is at least
equal to that of the relevant current-carrying
conductors.
N/A

Note 1: As a separating transformer is not a MAINS SUPPLY TRANSFORMER, it does not
require more than BASIC INSULATION.
Note 2: Limitation of output power is not explained in CAN/CSA-E61558-2-1 and the
RATED output power is defined by the fuse in the installation and by the allowable
power supply cable used. However, the characteristics of the separating transformer
need to be carefully selected, taking into account the variations in the load current of
the ME SYSTEM to ensure that the voltage supplied to the various items of the ME
SYSTEM remains within the limits specified for the equipment.
Note 3: For additional details refer to the Canadian Electrical Code, Part I,
Diagrams 1 and 2.

Use of uncertainty of measurement for decisions on conformity (decision rule) :
No decision rule is specified by the IEC standard, when comparing the measurement result with the
applicable limit according to the specification in that standard. The decisions on conformity are made
without applying the measurement uncertainty (“simple acceptance” decision rule, previously known as
“accuracy method”).
Other: … (to be specified, for example when required by the standard or client, or if national
accreditation requirements apply)
Information on uncertainty of measurement:
The uncertainties of measurement are calculated by the laboratory based on application of criteria given
by OD-5014 for test equipment and application of test methods, decision sheets and operational
procedures of IECEE.
IEC Guide 115 provides guidance on the application of measurement uncertainty principles and applying
the decision rule when reporting test results within IECEE scheme, noting that the reporting of the
measurement uncertainty for measurements is not necessary unless required by the test standard or
customer.
Calculations leading to the reported values are on file with the NCB and testing laboratory that conducted
the testing.

authorized by the respective NCBs that own these marks.

4 PRINCIPLES
4.1.1 The MANUFACTURER shall establish, document,
implement and maintain a USABILITY
ENGINEERING PROCESS, as defined in Clause
5, to provide SAFETY for the PATIENT, USER and
others. The PROCESS shall address USER
interactions with the MEDICAL DEVICE according
to the ACCOMPANYING DOCUMENTATION
Usability validation report (A-
TCF-5-040)
P
USABILITY ENGINEERING activities for a
MEDICAL DEVICE shall be planned, carried out,
and documented by personnel competent on the
basis of appropriate education, training, skills or
experience.
Usability engineering report (A-
TCF-5-056)
P
Where a documented product realization PROCESS
exists, such as that described in Clause 7 of ISO
13485:2016, it shall incorporate the appropriate
parts of or reference the USABILITY ENGINEERING
PROCESS .
Usability engineering report (A-
TCF-5-056)
P
Compliance with this subclause to exist when the
requirements of this International Standard have
been fulfilled.
P
4.1.2 To reduce use-related RISK, the
MANUFACTURER shall use one or more of the
following options, in the priority listed (as required
by ISO 14971:2019, 7.1):
Usability validation report (A-
TCF-5-040)
P
a) inherently safe design and manufacture; P
b) protective measures in the MEDICAL DEVICE
itself or in the manufacturing PROCESS; and
P
c) information for SAFETY and, where appropriate,
training to USERS.
P
4.1.3 When, in accordance with the priorities of 4.1.2,
information for SAFETY is used as a RISK CONTROL
measure, the MANUFACTURER shall subject this
information to the USABILITY ENGINEERING PROCESS
Usability validation plan (A-
TCF-5-039)
Usability validation report (A-
TCF-5-040)
P
4.2 The results of the USABILITY ENGINEERING PROCESS
are stored in the USABILITY ENGINEERING FILE ............. :
Usability engineering report (A-
TCF-5-056)
P
4.3 The level of effort and the choice of methods and
tools used to perform the USABILITY ENGINEERING
PROCESS vary based on:
Usability engineering report (A-
TCF-5-056)
P
a) the size and COMPLEXITY of the USER INTERFACE P
b) the SEVERITY of the HARM associated with the use
of the MEDICAL DEVICE
P
c) the extent or complexity of the USE SPECIFICATION P
d) the presence of USER INTERFACE OF UNKNOWN
PROVENANCE
P

National Differences
-- The following deviations are intended to meet Canadian product requirements and
to align with the Canadian Electrical Code, Part I.
IEC 60601-1-6:2010+A1:2013+A2:2020 (edition 3.2) forms the basis for CAN/CSA-
C22.2 No. 60601-1-6, which contains the following deviations in addition to those
shown in CAN/CSA-C22.2 No. 60601-1:14.
[Replace all references to “IEC 60601-1” with “CAN/CSA-C22.2 No. 60601-1”]
P
1.1 [Add the following paragraph]

1. Safety Information
1.1 Notice
For the improvement of Product performance, supplementation and the follow-up of information the
contents of this manual are subject to change without prior notice.
Please, note that our company bears no responsibility for accidental damage nor will we be obligated
to provide warranty service for any damage to equipment due to user error. Please, follow the
instructions in this manual closely. Become familiar with the safety precautions and usage procedures
for this Product. Note that the Product may differ slightly from the contents of this manual, depending
on individual Product specifications.
This manual is written in English. In case of EU language translation required, please contact
manufacturer customer service information in manual or local distributor. Translation will be provided
based by this manual

1.3 Warning
Symbols Descriptions
Environment of Use and Storage
⚫ Follow the specified process of operation instruction written in this manual
for the safety of the users and patients.
⚫ Local regulations should be reviewed before using to the pregnant or those
who have limitations in X-rays due to health issues. Make sure to check the
conditions of X-ray irradiation in advance.
Connection
⚫ Do not connect the detector with anything other than specified. Otherwise, it
may result in fire or electric shock.
⚫ To avoid the risk of electric shock, this detector must only be connected to
supply mains with protective earth.
⚫ Avoid installing the system in such way that it is difficult for the operator to
disconnect the appliance plug.
⚫ Do not touch Signal Input Part/Signal Output Part and the patient
simultaneously. There is a risk of electric shock from current leakage.
⚫ Additional equipment connected to medical electrical equipment must
comply with the respective IEC or ISO standards. Furthermore, all
configurations shall comply with the requirements for medical electrical
systems. Anybody connecting additional equipment to medical electrical
equipment configures a medical system and is therefore responsible that
the system complies with the requirements for medical electrical systems.
Attention is drawn to the fact that local laws take priority over the above-
mentioned requirements.
⚫ Equipment connected to the detector and in the patient environment must
be powered from a medically-isolated power source or must be a medically-
isolated device. Equipment powered from a non-isolated source can result
in chassis leakage currents exceeding safe levels. Chassis leakage current
created by an accessory or device connected to a non-isolated outlet may
add to the chassis leakage current of the detector.
⚫ Do not install at the building power system prospective short-circuit current
exceeding 35 A.
Handling
⚫ Always be sure to keep checking the condition of the system and the patient
to ensure they are normal during the use of the detector. If any problem is
found, take appropriate measures, such as stopping the operation of the
detector, as required.
⚫ Never disassemble or modify the detector as it may result in fire or electric
shock.
⚫ Also, since the detector incorporates parts that may cause electric shocks
and other hazardous parts, touching them may cause death or serious
injury.
⚫ Do not hit or drop the detector. The detector may be damaged if it receives
a strong jolt, which may result in fire or electric shock if the detector is used
without being repaired

9
When Problem Occurs
⚫ Should any of the following occur, immediately remove the battery from the
detector, unplug the power supply cord from the AC outlet, and contact
H&abyz Customer Service team or authorized distributor.
➢ When there is smoke, odd smell or abnormal sound.
➢ When liquid has been spilled into the detector or a metal object has
entered through an opening.
➢ When the detector has been dropped and it is damaged.
Error Massages
⚫ Messages about occur errors when using the detector are not output
directly from the software.
⚫ It is provided in text format for use in upper-level software (see Section 1.5).
⚫ For error message contents and actions, refer to the relevant upper level
software manual..
⚫ If the Upper Level Software Manual does not work, contact your H&abyz
Customer Service team or authorized dealer.
Security
⚫ The ADD protects all the transmitted data by applying such as WPA,
WPAPSK, WPA2, WPA2, WPA2PSK, WPAPSK+TKIP, etc.
⚫ The ADD restricts random access by setting ID / PW when connecting to
wireless network.
⚫ In the event of a threat related to the cybersecurity of the equipment and
software, immediately stop the equipment or software from working and
contact the manufacturer or distributor to take the necessary action.
Maintenance and Inspection
⚫ For safety reasons, be sure to turn off the power of the detector when the
following inspections are going to be performed. Otherwise, it may result in
electric shock.
➢ Make sure to turn off the detector, remove the battery, and unplug the
power cable from the AC outlet before cleaning.
➢ Do not use any type of solvent, such as benzene. Otherwise, fire or
electric shock may result.
➢ Wear waterproof gloves to protect your hands from direct contact with
IPA (Isopropyl-alcohol) or any other liquid.
➢ Maintenance of the detector should be done by an authorized service
provider. If problem still cannot be corrected, it may result in fire or
electric shock.
Patients Contact
⚫ The surface with a decoration sheet of the detector is available for direct
patient contact.

10
1.4 Caution
Symbols Descriptions
User Requirements
⚫ This equipment should be only operated by users who have received
professional medical education and training, such as physicians,
radiologists, and other medical specialists.
⚫ Federal law (USA) restricts this device to sale by or on the order of a
physician
Environment of Use and Storage
⚫ Do not install the detector in a location with the conditions listed below.
Otherwise, it may result in failure or malfunction, cause fire or injury.
➢ Close to facilities where water is used.
➢ Where it will be exposed to direct sunlight.
➢ Close to air-conditioner or ventilation equipment.
➢ Close to heat source such as a heater.
➢ Prone to vibration
➢ Dusty environment.
➢ Saline or sulfurous environment.
➢ High temperature or humidity.
⚫ Do not place the storage case in a location with the conditions listed
below
➢ Where someone might get their foot caught in the cable.
➢ Where the cable of the detector unit will be strongly pulled when the
detector is put into the case, otherwise, the cable may be damaged,
resulting in fire or electric shock.
⚫ Make sure to avoid prolonged contact with a patient for safe use.(Max.10
min). Highest temp of the surface: 47 ℃ (when the surrounding temp is
40 ℃)
Handling
⚫ In order to prevent infection, please wipe the CFRP (Carbon Fiber
Reinforced Plastic) with a soft cloth moistened with IPA (Isopropyl-
alcohol) liquid. Wear waterproof gloves to protect your hands from direct
contact with IPA or any other liquid.
⚫ For safety’s sake, keep all the cables unplugged and the battery
removed when the detector is not in use.
⚫ Make sure to use the battery in the conditions mentioned below.
Otherwise, it may result in a fire, injury, failure, or malfunction.
➢ Be sure to recharge the battery by using the ADD detector or the
battery recharger provided by H&abyz.
➢ If the battery is needed to be stored for a long period, battery should
be removed from the application and stored in a place where
humidity and temperature are low.
➢ While the battery is charged, used and stored, keep it away from

11
object materials with static electric chargers.
➢ If the terminals of the battery become dirty, wipe with a dry cloth
before using the battery.
➢ Be sure to use the battery in the environment designated by
H&abyz. Otherwise, the life of battery can be short
➢ Stop using the battery if the battery becomes abnormally hot,
disorder, discoloration, deformation, or abnormal conditions is
detected during use, charge, or storage.
➢ Don't short circuit (+) and (-) terminals with metallic object
intentionally.
➢ Not be sure to touch liquid on the surface of the battery.
➢ Don't pierce the battery with a sharp object such as a needle, screw
drivers.
➢ Do not hit the battery with heavy objects.
➢ Don't step on the battery and throw or drop the battery on the hard
floor to avoid mechanical shock.
➢ Don't disassemble the battery or modify the battery design including
electric circuit.
⚫ Make sure to use the battery in the conditions mentioned below.
Otherwise, it may result in a fire, injury, failure, or malfunction.
➢ When using battery recharger, always use the battery provided by
H&abyz..
➢ When using battery recharger, Be sure to use Adapter Provided by
H&abyz.
➢ When moving battery recharger, always separate the power and
battery pack
➢ When using battery recharger, Always be cautious about touching
liquid, impurities. In case of short trouble.
➢ Do not disassemble the battery recharger.
➢ When using battery recharger, be sure to comply with the user
environment. The battery provided by H&abyz can be down and the
durability can be shorter.
➢ Be sure to use battery recharger in the Control Room. This battery
recharger is not designed to use in the Examination Room.
➢ When not using the battery recharger for a long time. Always do
separate the battery recharger from the Power.
➢ When inserting the battery to the battery recharger, Be careful of
being caught clothes or impurities.
Location of Cables
⚫ Make sure all cables are located so that they cannot be stepped on,
tripped over, or otherwise subjected to damage or stress.

Maintenance and Inspection
⚫ For safety reasons, be sure to inspect the detector before using it. In
addition, carry out a regular inspection at least once a year.
⚫ If the detector is defective, do not disassemble the detector randomly.
Maintenance of the detector should be done by an authorized service
provider. Please contact H&abyz Customer Service team or authorized
agent.
⚫ Be sure to check the user’s manual for replaceable components.

1.5 Safety Information
⚫ General Safety
Preparation
➢ Be sure to connect the cables to the proper connectors. Otherwise, the detector may
malfunction or may be damaged.
➢ The battery should be equipped at a specified location. Otherwise, the detector may
malfunction or be damaged.
Handling
➢ Handle the detector carefully, as it may become damaged if it is hit, dropped, or receives
a strong jolt.
➢ Be sure to use the detector on a flat place so it will not bend. Otherwise, the detector may
be damaged.
➢ Be sure to check the detector daily and confirm that it works properly. Sudden heating of
the room in cold areas will cause condensation to form on the detector. In this case, wait
until condensation disappears before performing exposure. If the detector is used with
condensation formed on it, problems may occur in the quality of the detector. When an
air-conditioner is going to be used, be sure to raise/lower the temperature gradually so
that a difference in temperature in the room and in the detector does not occur, to prevent
forming of condensation. Follow the recommended proper room temp.
➢ Do not use the detector near devices generating a strong magnetic field. Doing so may
produce image noise or artifacts.
➢ Keep the connectors free from being in contact with the patient.
➢ Connectors are intended to be connected to an external device and must follow IEC
standards.

14
➢ Do not apply excessive weight to the detector. Otherwise, the detector may be damaged
➢ Use a Weight Distribution Cap when weight of a patient is concentrated on one particular
point.
<Uniform Load : uniform distribution of weight>
<Local Load : concentration of weight >
Disinfection and Cleaning
➢ Do not spray disinfectants or detergents on the detector.
➢ Make sure to turn off the detector, remove the battery and unplug the power cable from
the AC outlet before cleaning.

➢ Do not use any type of solvent, such as benzene. Otherwise, fire may result.
➢ Wear waterproof gloves to protect your hands from direct contact with disinfectants or
detergents.
⚫ Electrical Safety
➢ In compliance with IEC 60601-1, this medical equipment complies with the requirements
for Safety class I
➢ This system must be used in an environment complying with the requirements of the IEC.

15
⚫ EMC (Electromagnetic Compatibility)
➢ Do not use any wireless devices, including cellular phones, near the system. All wireless
devices, whether they comply with the EMC standard or not, may emit electromagnetic
interferences and cause the system to malfunction when they are used nearby.
➢ See Section (10. EMC Declaration)
⚫ Solution for error
“Connect Error”
➢ Description: connection unavailable between the detector and the software.
➢ Cause: network disconnection or power supply removal.
➢ Solution: In case of connection error, the “Connect Error” message is passed to the upper level
software. Check the detector power supply and network cable connection. If necessary, replace
the power supply, power cable and network cable.

16
“Image Processing Error”
➢ Description: Unremovable noise on the acquired image when pre-processing.
➢ Cause: when the provided calibration file is changed or removed, a number of noise or line is
occurred on the acquired image.
➢ Solution: Check the provided calibration file and if it is changed or removed, reobtain the
calibration file and apply.

[ figure 1 – 2 normal image ]

2. Product Introduction and Specification
2.1 Product Features
The ADD are wired or wireless digital flat panel detectors that have been designed for faster, more
streamlined approach to digital radiography systems. The ADD detector utilize a combination of
propriety TFT glass and scintillators(CsI), and those and electronics are housed in one package. The
detectors support an auto exposure detection technology that allows the detectors to be used without
generator integration.
The flat panel sensors of the ADD are fabricated using thin film technology based on amorphous
silicon technology. Electronically, the sensors are much like conventional photodiode arrays. Each

20
pixel in the array consists of a light‐sensing photodiode and a switching Thin Film Transistor (TFT) in
the same electronic circuit. Amorphous silicon photodiodes are sensitive to visible light, with a
response curve roughly comparable to human vision. The sensitivity of amorphous silicon
photodiodes peaks in green wavelengths, well matched to scintillators such as CsI. The response has
the excellent linearity of a charge‐integrating-biased photodiode.
Indications for use
ADD (Digital Flat Panel X-Ray Detector) is indicated for digital imaging solution designed for
providing general radiographic diagnosis of human anatomy targeting both adult and children. It is
intended to replace film based radiographic diagnostic systems. Not to be used for mammography

2.3 Performance Principle
To obtain an X-ray image with any type of X-ray image detector the part of the patient to be X-rayed
is placed between the X-ray source and the image receptor to produce a shadow of the internal
structure of that particular part of the body. X-rays are partially attenuated by dense tissues such as
bone, and pass more easily through soft tissues. Areas where the X-rays strike darken when
developed, causing bones to appear lighter than the surrounding soft tissue.
Indirect type detectors are made up of a scintillator to convert x-rays to visible light and a phosphor
to convert the light to electrons, which is read by a TFT array. The TFT array consists of a sheet of
glass covered with a thin layer of silicon that is in an amorphous or disordered state. At a microscopic
scale, the silicon has been imprinted with millions of transistors arranged in a highly ordered array, like
the grid on a sheet of graph paper. Each of these thin-film transistors (TFTs) is attached to a light-
absorbing photodiode making up an individual pixel. Photons striking the photodiode are converted
into two carriers of electrical charge, called electron-hole pairs. Since the number of charge carriers
produced will vary with the intensity of incoming light photons, an electrical pattern is created that can
be swiftly converted to a voltage and then a digital signal, which is interpreted by a computer to
produce a digital image.

25
2.4 Intended patient population
Radiographic imaging of human body parts such as head, Chest, spinal, abdominal, particular, hand,
foot and other internal organs.
a) Age: Available all people
b) Weight: not relevant
c) Height: not relevant
d) Nationality: multiple
e) Patient group/state: No specification
d) Applications parts: Part of body
f) Disease: Radiographic imaging of human body parts such as head, Chest, spinal, abdominal,
particular, hand, foot and other internal organs.

3. Installation and Calibration
3.1 Installation

➢ Click “Install” to start installation.

45

➢ Microsoft Visual Studio Package is necessary to use Abyz Acquisition Software and
Viewer. Select the checkbox "동의함(A)" and click "설치(I)".

46
➢ Click “Close” when the installation is finished.
➢ Click “OK” when Hn_DR_Install is completed.

47
⚫ Product Set-Up
1) Connection methods of each operation mode
➢ AED Mode (Auto Exposure Detection Mode)
The user can acquire images without additional connection between the X-ray
system, which is already installed, and the detector. When X-rays are exposed by a
exposure switch, the detector detects the X-rays that are absorbed without external
exposure signals and convert them into digital signals.
Converted digital data is delivered to PC via AP (Access Point) or main cable, and PC
converts the delivered data into images to show it on the monitor.
The minimum dose is 50 kVp and 5 ms (90 mA or more) under conditions where the
SID is 100 cm and there is no phantom with 21 mm Al filter applied. The minimum
dose may change depending on the detailed irradiation conditions.
※ Object, PC, X-ray System are not included in this component.

48
➢ Normal Mode (with Switch Box)
The user can acquire images by connecting Switch Box to X-ray system that is already
installed. Normal Mode is to send exposure signals to PC and X-ray System using
Switch Box and a separate exposure switch. By pressing the exposure switch connected
to Switch Box, the detector is activated and ‘Ready’ sign can be seen. When prepared,
the detector delivers exposure signals to X-ray System.
The detector converts absorbed x-ray to digital data, deliver it to PC via AP (Access
Point) or main cable, and PC converts the delivered digital data into images to show it
on the monitor.
※ Object, PC, X-ray System are not included in this component.
• The detector operates in a wireless state when using a battery, and in
a wired state when using a data cable.

49
2) PC Set-Up
➢ Set-Up the Network as below
[Network Connection] > [Local Area Connection] > Click “Properties”
➢ Select [Internet Protocol Version 4(TCP/IP)] > Click “Properties

50
➢ Select [Use the following IP address], and then enter the IP address the Detector IP
address.
• Abyz Detector’s default IP address is 192.168.197.80, Also you can
use 192.168.197.80 ~ 192.168.197.200 detector IP. H&Abyz
recommends 192.168.197.2 ~ 192.168.197.70 for PC IP address and
255.255.255.0 for Subnet mask.

51
⚫ Image Acquisition software (XAS_W) set up
➢ Connect the detector and turn the power on.
➢ If the connected detector IP address is different from the IP address, enter the
detector IP address connected to the "Detector IP Address" and click "set" button.

52
➢ Run “XAS_W.exe” which is in “C:\XAS_W”. Once the detector is connected to PC
successfully, the network info sign shall turn from red ‘X’ to green ‘✓’
➢ Verify that the software "Com Port" is set to the same value after verifying the port
number of the Switch Box USB cable connected to the PC in the Device Manager.

53
➢ After checking connection, select Trigger Mode (Trigger Mode) out of Normal Mode

and AED Mode (Auto Exposure Detection Mode). If it is successful, a pop-up shall
come on and the changed Trigger Mode (Trigger Mode) be shown in “Detector
Status”.

54
3.2 Calibration
Calibration shall be performed to acquire a proper image. The image will not be clear enough
without calibration.
• Calibration shall be performed once every one year for stabilized
detector condition.
⚫ Dark Image Acquisition
➢ Click "Get Dark" to get a Dark image on the "Calibration" tab. The "Preview" window
appears and acquires the Dark image. The acquired Dark image will be displayed in
the image file list.
• H&Abyz recommends to use the "Average Dark" option to enhance image
performance.
• If you select the "Average Dark" option, Dark images will be automatically

55
acquired to the number of "total dark frame" values.
• Dark image in AED Mode (Auto Exposure Detection Mode) is saved in the
below location.
C:\XAS_W\Cal_0\CalType0-AED\
• Dark image in Normal Mode is saved in the below location.
C:\ XAS_W \Cal_0\CalType0-NorTrg\
⚫ Bright Image Acquisition and Creation of calibration Point Image
➢ According to the Trigger Mode (Operation Mode), the bright image is acquired in
different ways.
➢ In AED Mode (Auto Exposure Detection Mode), click the “Get Bright” button of the
software to acquire the bright image. The bright images must be acquired at twenty
calibration points. The acquired bright images are shown in the image file list.

56
➢ In Normal Mode, without clicking the “Get Bright” on the software and uses the
Switch Box Exposure switch to acquire the bright image. The bright images must be
acquired at twenty calibration points. The acquired bright images are shown in the
image file list.
• H&Abyz recommends twenty calibration points such as written below. Some
artifact can be seen on images if the calibration points are not sufficient.
※ SID : 150
※ Cal point 1 ~ 17 : with Al 21mm filter
※ Cal point 18 ~ 20 : without Al 21mm filter

• In AED mode (Auto Exposure Detection Mode), each bright image must be
acquired at intervals of 30 seconds.
• In AED mode (Auto Exposure Detection Mode), X-ray shall be exposed within
30 seconds once the “Acquisition” button is clicked. Otherwise, the action will
be cancelled.
• In Normal Mode, the image is acquired using Switch Box Exposure switch,
not clicking “Get Bright” button.
• Do not expose X-ray when “Busy” message is displayed in “Preview” pop-up
window. Any Images can’t be acquired during “Busy” state although X-ray is
exposed. Expose X-ray when “Ready for Exposure” is shown up in “Preview”
window.

"*_OC_xxxx.raw" is automatically created. The acquired bright images are shown in
the image file list.

to PC condition. If customers repeatedly select others during
changing the detector, all detectors can be disconnected.

7. Maintenance
7.1 Cleaning
➢ Clean the detector with 70% IPA (Isopropyl-alcohol) when it is contaminated.
➢ Before cleaning the detector, turn off the power and separate the battery.
➢ Wear waterproof gloves to protect your hands from direct contact with IPA or any other
liquid.
➢ Do not pour or spray IPA directly on the detector. Use fabric or soft cloth moistened with
IPA to clean.
➢ Avoid getting IPA or any other liquid into the detector.
➢ After cleaning, wait until the IPA is dried completely.
7.2 Inspection
➢ In order to ensure that the detector is used safely and normally, please be sure to inspect
the product regularly before use.
➢ Please perform inspections based on the check list below.
Inspection List User Vendor Cycle
Check if cables are not damaged √ Daily
Check if plugs and connectors are not loose or damaged √ Daily
Check if cover or part is not damaged √ Daily
Check the LED indicator √ Daily
Re-Calibration √ Yearly

85

normal usage during the Warranty Period and H&abyz determines that such failure resulted from a
defect in materials or workmanship during the Warranty Period, then H&abyz, at its option, shall repair,
rebuild or adjust the affected parts.
H&abyz shall have no obligation for any defects to the extent that such defect arises out of (i) normal
and fair wear and tear or Product which has been modified without H&abyz’s approval, (ii) Product
which has not been installed in strict conformity to the H&abyz’s directions or which have been
subjected to electrical or other abuse, or damaged by improper handling, storage or use by Buyer or a
third party, (iii) use of Product in combination with devices or products not purchased from H&abyz;
(iv) use or application of Product in a field or in an environment for which such Product was not
designed or contemplated; (v) use of any parts or material not provided by H&abyz for warranty
service; or (vi) the third party’s maintenance not certified by H&abyz; or (vii) force majeure such as
natural disaster.
The remedies contained in this warranty are Buyer’s exclusive remedies. H&abyz shall not, in any
event or under any circumstances, be responsible for damages or other sums in excess of the total
purchase price actually paid by Buyer to Seller i.e., H&abyz or H&abyz’s authorized agent. Without
limiting the generality of the foregoing under no circumstance shall H&abyz be responsible or liable in
any regard with respect to damages from loss of use, loss of time, loss of data, inconvenience,
commercial loss, lost profits or savings, or other incidental, special or consequential damages claimed
by Buyer to arise out of the use or inability to use the Product, even if Buyer has been advised of the
possibility of such damages.
In the event that the product is returned to H&abyz after the warranty has expired, H&abyz reserves
the right to invoice a reasonable fee for the repair services provided to Buyer.
H&abyz shall make the sole final determination about whether the fail to perform occurred in normal
usage (under warranty) or not (excluded from warranty). If the authorized agent or the Buyer doesn’t
accept the result of H&abyz’s investigation, the burden of proof is on them.

10. EMC Declaration
⚫ Compliance Statement
This equipment complies with IEC 60601-1-2 EMC standards for medical devices.
This equipment needs special precautions regarding EMC and needs to be installed and put into
service according to the EMC information provided in the user manual.
Do not use any wireless devices, including cellular phones, near the system. All wireless devices,
whether they comply with the EMC standard or not, may emit electromagnetic interferences and
cause the system to malfunction when they are used nearby.
This equipment should not be used adjacent to or stacked with other equipment; if adjacent or
stacked use is necessary, the equipment should be tested and verified in order to ensure normal
operations in the configuration in which it will be used.
Changes or modifications not expressly approved by the party responsible for compliance could void
the user's authority to operate the equipment.
All interconnect cables to peripheral devices must be shielded and properly grounded, except when
technologically prohibited. Use of cables not properly shielded and grounded may result in the
equipment causing radio frequency interference.
The use of cables or accessories other than those specified may result in increased emissions or
decreased immunity.
Should any interference (EMC) be detected with other equipment, please position other equipment
away from this one.
When using this system on a patient with an implantable pacemaker or an implantable cardioverter
defibrillator, the patient must be informed that continuous X-ray exposure in pulse form may cause the
pacemaker or cardioverter defibrillator to malfunction.
When using this system, ensure that X-rays are not exposed directly onto the patient’s implantable
pacemaker or implantable cardioverter defibrillator, and that the exposure time is kept as short as
possible.

This equipment may be interfered with by other equipment, even if that other equipment complies with
CISPR EMISSION requirements.

91

NOTE 2 These guidelines may not apply in all situations. Electromagnetic propagation is affected by
absorption and reflection from structures, objects and people.
a Field strengths from fixed transmitters, such as base stations for radio (cellular/cordless) telephones and land
mobile radios, amateur radio, AM and FM radio broadcast and TV broadcast cannot be predicted theoretically
with accuracy. To assess the electromagnetic environment due to fixed RF transmitters, an electromagnetic site
survey should be considered. If the measured field strength in the location in which this Wireless Detector is used
exceeds the applicable RF compliance level above, this Wireless Detector should be observed to verify normal
operation. If abnormal performance is observed, additional measures may be necessary, such as re-orienting or
relocating this Wireless Detector.
b Over the frequency range 150 kHz to 80 MHz, field strengths should be less than 3 V/m.
⚫ Recommended separation distances between portable and mobile RF communications
equipment and this Wireless Detector
This Wireless Detector is intended for use in an electromagnetic environment in which radiated RF disturbances
are controlled. The customer or the user of this Wireless Detector can help prevent electromagnetic interference
by maintaining a minimum distance between portable and mobile RF communications equipment (transmitters)
and this Wireless Detector as recommended below, according to the maximum output power of the
communications equipment.

maximum output power rating of the transmitter in watts (W) according to the transmitter manufacturer.

11. Wired & Wireless Interface
Wired
Standard IEEE 802.3 compliance
Physical data rate 10/100/1000 BASE-T
Wireless
Standard IEEE 802.11 a/b/g/n Wi-Fi
Frequency 2.4GHz/5GHz dual
Bandwidth 20 MHz / 40MHz
MIMO 2X2
Modulation OFDM with BPSK, QPSK, 16 QAM, 64 QAM, DBPSK,
CCK
Security Open, WEP, WPA/WPA2 PSK, PWA/WPA2 Enterprise
Physical data rate IEEE 802.11a : 6-54Mbps
IEEE 802.11b : 1-11Mbps
IEEE 802.11g : 6-54Mbps
IEEE 802.11n : 6.5-300Mbps
Power Output (EIRP) For 2.4 GHz band : 13.80 dBm
For 5 GHz Lower sub-band : 14.76 dBm
For 5 GHz Higher sub-band : 12.39 dBm
⚫ Maximum wireless signal rate derived from IEEE standard specifications. Actual data throughput
will vary. Network conditions and environmental factors, including volume of network traffic,
building materials and construction, and network overhead, lower actual data throughput rate.
⚫ Recommended Maximum operable distance : 3m (From the Access Point)
⚫ Wireless Antenna: The module adopts the latest 802.11n Dual-Band technology (2.4Ghz and
5Ghz). The transmitter of the module is powered by host equipment (Detector). The antennas are
2 printed-dipole antennas.
⚫ Wireless module: 802.11 a/b/g/n modules are implemented. It supports 2T2R (2 transmit 2
receive) MIMO technology, which delivers throughput up to 300 Mbps.
⚫ The ADD restricts random access by setting ID / PW when connecting to the wires network.
⚫ All the transmission data are protected by applying encryption such as WEP, WPA/WPA2 PSK,
PWA/WPA2.
• Restriction of use of Wi-Fi using 5 GHz bands(5150 - 5350 MHz)
“In the EU, the Wi-Fi function in this equipment should not be used
outdoors.
• Do not connect any devices to the detector that is already in
network.

➢ Click “…” (in the red box) next to “Upload file” in the ‘’Settings’’ tab, and choose the
file to update and click “Update”. You may see the completion in the “Log” tab.

2. Troubleshooting
Problem Solution
When the detector is not turned on • check the battery charging status
• check the connection of data cable
When the power is off all of a sudden • check the remaining battery
• check the connection of data cable
When the network is disconnected • check the LAN cable connected to PC and power supply box
• check the network of WIFI router
• check if the IP address is "192.168.197.102 ~ 192.168.197.254" in
the internet protocol version 4 properties.
When a problem occurs on the image
acquired.
• check if there is any dust on the surface of the detector
• contact H&abyz Customer Service team or authorized distributor
when the problem is not solved after 30mins waiting.
